<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A new systematic methodology for the design of T-match based UHF-RFID tags is proposed. The great majority of commercial UHF-RFID tags are based on dipole antennas using a modification of a T-match network. The literature contains examples of models that describe the T-match, but they are not sufficiently accurate to synthesize the tag geometry. Using the proposed methodology, a global band UHF-RFID tag based on a folded dipole antenna and matched to the RFID integrated circuit by means of a T-match network is designed and fabricated. Very good agreement between the measured and simulated read range is achieved within the entire UHF-RFID band, which reveals that the proposed method is amenable for accurate analysis and synthesis of T-match based UHF-RFID tags.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) is a rapidly developing technology that provides wireless identification and tracking capability. Particularly, passive ultra-high frequency (UHF) RFID systems are very attractive in comparison with passive RFID regulated systems using low frequency (LF) and high frequency (HF) bands, since they can provide superior read range, fast reading and enhanced information storage ability <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. The regulated UHF-RFID bands vary in the different world regions, including frequencies between 840 MHz and 960 MHz. More specifically, RFID is operated at 840–845 MHz in China, at 866–869 MHz in Europe, at 902–928 MHz in USA and at 950–956 MHz in Japan. Therefore, the design of inlay tags able to cover the whole regulated UHF bands (i.e., global band tags) becomes an important challenge.</p><p>A passive UHF-RFID system consists of a reader and a tag, which includes an antenna matched to an application specific integrated circuit (ASIC) chip. Generally, the chip impedance is capacitive, thereby requiring the antenna impedance to be inductive in order to obtain a proper impedance matching (conjugate matching). Several techniques for achieving conjugate matching can be found in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. However, most commercial UHF-RFID tags are based on dipole antennas using some variant of a T- match network <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. The T-match connection was first proposed by Uda <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, and more recently explained in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> as an effective shunt-matching technique. Although it was initially analyzed as a general form of a cylindrical folded dipole, the Uda model has been applied to design planar structures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> and even RFID tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. However, many approximations are assumed when planar conductor shapes are considered <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. Moreover, by this means, only a special case of the T-match structure can be used to design RFID tags, the embedded T-match, that is constructed by embedding the T-match structure into the antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. This is the main drawback since most commercially available T-match based tags have more complex geometries which cannot be analyzed by means of this planar model. An example of these tags is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, where the T-match network has a loop shape and is located at the center of the tag. In order to overcome this problem, some efforts to deviate from Uda classic analysis and focus on a circuit-based approach have been made <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>. In these works, equivalent-circuit models of a dipole antenna (only valid over a relatively small frequency range near resonance) matched to the chip by means of a T-match have been developed. Nevertheless, the synthesis process of the tags from the obtained circuits is not fully explained.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Example of a UHF-RFID commercial tag based on the T-match network (Alien ALN-9640).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In this paper, a new and very simple systematic method for the design and synthesis of global band UHF-RFID tags based on the T-match network is presented. Such method is based on a new equivalent-circuit model approach. Moreover, the frequency limits related to the validity of the presented approach are studied, and the dependence of the achieved tag bandwidth with the antenna impedance is also discussed. To illustrate the potential of the approach, an RFID tag is designed and synthetized through this method and the read range of the fabricated prototype is measured.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Equivalent Circuit Model of T-Match Based Tags: New Approach and Requirements</h2></div><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>(a) Balanced equivalent-circuit model of a T-match based UHF-RFID tag from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>, and (b) unbalanced equivalent-circuit model reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The T-match structure, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, is the most common matching network used for the efficient matching of UHF-RFID tags. Since this network is electrically small at the UHF-RFID regulated bands (840–960 MHz), a lumped-element equivalent-circuit model can be considered. Moreover, it is well known that the input impedance of a UHF-RFID chip can be modeled by a parallel combination of a resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">C_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a>. Thus, a circuit model for the T-match structure cascaded to a commercial RFID chip can be obtained, which is of special interest for tag design. Some efforts to obtain an equivalent-circuit model for the T-match network cascaded to the chip can be found in the literature. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>, the circuit diagram shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a> is proposed, whereas in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a> this balanced circuit is reduced to an unbalanced version, depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>. Although this circuit is complete and reasonably accurate, the authors in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a> transformed the matching circuit from a series-shunt connection of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-15" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">L_{e}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-22" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">L_{h}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> into a shunt-series connection with a scaled load impedance. This allows reformulating the tag antenna and matching circuit problem into a classical two stage bandpass filter. The main drawback of such approach is the difficulty to synthesize the tag antenna and matching circuit, once the circuit model is tuned. Moreover, the authors do not give details about how to synthesize the presented tags from the circuit model.<p></p><p>

= G_{\rm eq} + jB_{\rm eq} = {1\over R_{\rm eq}} - j {1\over \omega L_{\rm eq}} &amp;\hbox{(3)} }</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{G_{\rm in} &amp; = {2L_{2}^{2} R_{a}\over \vert {Z_{a}} \vert^{2} ({L_{1} + L_{2}})^{2} + 4\omega^{2}L_{1}^{2} L_{2}^{2} + 4\omega \chi_{a} L_{1} L_{2} ({L_{1} + L_{2}})} &amp;\hbox{(1)}\cr B_{\rm in} &amp; = {- \left[{\vert {Z_{a}} \vert^{2} ({L_{1} + L_{2}}) + 4\omega^{2} L_{2}^{2} L_{1} + 2\omega \chi_{a} ({L_{2}^{2} + 2L_{1} L_{2}})} \right]\over \omega \left[{\vert {Z_{a}} \vert^{2} ({L_{1} + L_{2}})^{2} + 4\omega^{2}L_{1}^{2} L_{2}^{2} + 4\omega \chi _{a} L_{1} L_{2} ({L_{1} + L_{2}})} \right]} &amp;\hbox{(2)}\cr Y_{\rm eq} &amp; = G_{\rm eq} + jB_{\rm eq} = {1\over R_{\rm eq}} - j {1\over \omega L_{\rm eq}} &amp;\hbox{(3)} }</span></span></disp-formula>In this work, due to the symmetry of T-match based tags and the differential mode excitation, forced by the chip, the electric wall concept has been used in order to obtain an equivalent-circuit model (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>). The required values of the circuit elements can be obtained by considering only one-half of the network (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>). It can be observed that the circuit cascaded between the chip and the antenna is an inductive transformer <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a>. Thus, the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> can be modeled by the circuit depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Design and Synthesis of T-Match Based Tags</h2></div><p>A systematic methodology for the design and synthesis of a global band T-match based tag is presented in this section. Let us consider the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>, assuming that conditions <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> are well satisfied, as a model for T-match based tags. The central frequency of the operating band is chosen to be the intermediate frequency of the UHF-RFID band, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1403" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; Then, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1412" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; It is clear that, for a given chip and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1483" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1498"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1499"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; However, in spite of the possibility of satisfying conditions <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> by means of an antenna with a complex impedance, resonant antennas designed at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1504" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1505"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1506"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1507" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1508"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1509"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1510" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are very good candidates for using the proposed circuit approach. This is because, regardless of the considered chip, condition <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> will be easily satisfied in the vicinity of the antenna resonance frequency since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1511" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1512"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1513"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1514" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">χ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1515"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1516"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1517" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">\chi _{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> approaches zero. Therefore, the proposed equivalent-circuit model will predict the frequency response of the designed tag in a wider bandwidth when a resonant antenna is considered.</p><p>

overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.338em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) as a function of the antenna resistance, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1525" role="math" style="width: 1.524em; Notice that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1532" role="math" style="width: 1.789em; Let us consider the particular case of using a resonant tag antenna designed to exhibit a purely resistive impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1549" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1556" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; It is important to point out that even if conditions <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> are very well satisfied, a frequency shift of the tag resonance and a reduction of the matching level (with respect to conjugate matching) at this frequency are expected, as long as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1563" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> differs from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1570" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.646em -999.997em); However, this frequency shift can be avoided by taking it into account in the T-match design stage, and the matching level at the tag resonance can be predicted. Let us see how this is possible by means of an analysis of the power reflection coefficient of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>, given by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_3">[17]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_3">[18]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn10" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1593" role="math" style="width: 100%; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1868" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1869" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1870"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1871"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1872" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1873" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1874" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1875"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1876"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1877" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1878" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1879" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1880"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.381em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1882"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1883"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1884" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.721em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1885"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1886"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1887" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1888"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1889" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1890"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1891"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1892" style="font-size: 70.7%; This corresponds to a frequency shift of the tag resonance, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \omega = 2 \pi \Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1894" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1895"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1896" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1897" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1898" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1899" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1900" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">π<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1901" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1902" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\Delta \omega = 2 \pi \Delta f</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, towards higher frequencies, which depends only upon the antenna resistance, for a given chip (see <a ref-type="app" anchor="app1a" class="fulltext-link">Appendix A</a>). Such shift is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> in the case of considering four different commercial chips <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_3">[19]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_3">[20]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_3">[21]</a>. It can be seen that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1903" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1904"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1905" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1906" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\Delta f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decreases as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1907" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1908"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1909"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1911"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1912"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1913" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> approaches the chip resistance, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1914" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1918"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1919"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1920" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">R_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and becomes higher as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1921" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1922"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1923"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1932"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1933"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1934" style="font-size: 70.7%; (The case when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} &gt; R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1935" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1944" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1945"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1946"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1947" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">R_{a} &gt; R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not necessary to be discussed, since the presented method requires that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} \leq R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1948" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1955" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≤</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1956" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1957" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; Moreover, a reduction of the matching level (with respect to conjugate matching) will take place at this frequency, as long as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1961" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1965"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1966"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1967" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1972"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1973"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1974" style="font-size: 70.7%; From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a> it follows that the exact expression for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1975" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1978" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1979"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1980"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1981" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1982" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">G_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> evaluated at the tag resonance <disp-formula id="deqn11" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{G_{\rm eq} &amp;= {2R_{a} \omega_{0}^{4} C_{c}^{2}\over R_{a} R_{c} \omega_{0}^{4} C_{c}^{2} + ({\omega_{0} + \Delta \omega})^{2} \left({1 - \sqrt{{R_{a}}/{R_{c}}}}\right)^{2}}\quad&amp;\hbox{(11)} }</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1983" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; Then, by evaluating <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a> at the tag resonance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(B = 0)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2128" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; Obviously, the same power reflection coefficient as in the previous case (where a constant antenna impedance value was considered) will be achieved at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0} + \Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2169" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; Furthermore, it can be demonstrated from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a> that the minimum power reflection coefficient occurs roughly at that frequency when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2192" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; Notice that if conditions <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8-9" href="#deqn8-9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> are satisfied, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2224" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; The shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2476" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block;
