width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-111">\eqalignno{\vert {Z_{a}} \vert &amp; \gg {1\over n\omega_{0} C_{c}} &amp;\hbox{(14)}\cr \vert {\chi_{a}} \vert &amp; \leq \cases{{1\over \omega_{0} C_{c}} &amp; ${\rm if}\ 1 \leq n \leq {3\over 2}$ \cr {1\over 2\omega_{0} C_{c} ({n - 1})}&amp; ${\rm if}\ n &gt; {3\over 2}$} &amp;\hbox{(15)} }</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{\vert {Z_{a}} \vert &amp; \gg {1\over n\omega_{0} C_{c}} &amp;\hbox{(14)}\cr \vert {\chi_{a}} \vert &amp; \leq \cases{{1\over \omega_{0} C_{c}} &amp; ${\rm if}\ 1 \leq n \leq {3\over 2}$ \cr {1\over 2\omega_{0} C_{c} ({n - 1})}&amp; ${\rm if}\ n &gt; {3\over 2}$} &amp;\hbox{(15)} }</span></span></disp-formula> where, it has been considered <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega\approx\omega_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">\omega\approx\omega_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\omega_{0} - \Delta \omega)\approx \omega_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">(\omega_{0} - \Delta \omega)\approx \omega_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, since variations of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">\omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> relative to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega _{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">\omega _{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are less than 7% within the whole UHF-RFID band and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \omega \ll \omega_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">\Delta \omega \ll \omega_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Notice that condition <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> does not play any role to achieve complex conjugate matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\chi_{a} = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">\chi_{a} = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at this frequency (this condition will be used in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3c" class="fulltext-link">Section III.C</a> to discuss the frequency range of validity of the proposed circuit approach). However, expression <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> lead to a simple condition, in which the required antenna resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} (f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">R_{a} (f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> depends only upon the RFID chip and the intermediate frequency as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} (f_{0}) \gg 1/(\omega_{0}^{2} C_{c}^{2}R _{c})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">R_{a} (f_{0}) \gg 1/(\omega_{0}^{2} C_{c}^{2}R _{c})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Therefore, the greater the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} (f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">R_{a} (f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the better satisfied the required condition. However, since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">R_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is forced to be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{c}/2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-123">R_{c}/2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-124">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as indicated before, it follows from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a> that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} (f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">R_{a} (f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> must be less than or equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Hence, it can be concluded that the presented approach is valid at the intermediate frequency, if the antenna resistance accomplishes <disp-formula id="deqn16" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{1\over \omega_{0}^{2} C_{c}^{2} R_{c}} \ll R_{a} ({f_{0}}) \leq R_{c} \eqno{\hbox{(16)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-127">{1\over \omega_{0}^{2} C_{c}^{2} R_{c}} \ll R_{a} ({f_{0}}) \leq R_{c} \eqno{\hbox{(16)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{1\over \omega_{0}^{2} C_{c}^{2} R_{c}} \ll R_{a} ({f_{0}}) \leq R_{c} \eqno{\hbox{(16)}}</span></span></disp-formula> Notice that condition <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn16" href="#deqn16" class="fulltext-link">(16)</a> forces <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(R_{c} C_{c})^{2} \gg 1/ \omega_{0}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-128">(R_{c} C_{c})^{2} \gg 1/ \omega_{0}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is well satisfied by the typical values of the RFID integrated circuits available on the market today, such as Impinj Monza 5, Impinj Monza X-2K Dura, Alien Higgs 3, Alien Higgs 4 and NXP UCODE G2XM <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_3a">[19]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_3a">[20]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_3a">[21]</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Tag Bandwidth Related to the Antenna Impedance</h3><p>Let us now demonstrate that a degradation of the maximum achievable tag bandwidth, by means of the proposed equivalent-circuit approach and considering conjugate matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-129-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-129">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, will be mainly determined by the derivative of the antenna resistance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-130-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-130">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It was demonstrated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_3b">[22]</a> that the optimum equivalent-circuit network necessary for bandwidth broadening in single resonant UHF-RFID tags with conjugate matching is a parallel combination of an inductor and a resistor cascaded to the chip, according to the Bode's limit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_3b">[23]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_3b">[24]</a>. However, the proposed circuit approach consists of a parallel combination of an inductor and a frequency dependent resistor, cascaded to the chip. Hence, bandwidth degradation with respect to the optimum will be obtained as long as the conductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-131-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-131">G_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> differs from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2 G_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-132-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-132">2 G_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In a first order approximation, this reduction of the tag bandwidth is determined by the frequency derivative of the antenna resistance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and it does not depend on the frequency derivative of the antenna reactance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\chi _{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-134">\chi _{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, since this term is cancelled. This result is deduced from the first-order Taylor expansion of the conductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-135">G_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, obtained from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a>, in the vicinity of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-136">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <disp-formula id="deqn17" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq} = 2G_{\rm chip} \left({1 - {R_{a} ^{\prime}(f_{0})\over R_{a} (f_{0})} ({f - f_{0}})} \right) \eqno{\hbox{(17)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-137">G_{\rm eq} = 2G_{\rm chip} \left({1 - {R_{a} ^{\prime}(f_{0})\over R_{a} (f_{0})} ({f - f_{0}})} \right) \eqno{\hbox{(17)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">G_{\rm eq} = 2G_{\rm chip} \left({1 - {R_{a} ^{\prime}(f_{0})\over R_{a} (f_{0})} ({f - f_{0}})} \right) \eqno{\hbox{(17)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}'(f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-138">R_{a}'(f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the frequency derivative of the antenna resistance evaluated at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Notice that, for a given value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} (f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">R_{a} (f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the further <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} '(f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">R_{a} '(f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is from zero, the further <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-142">G_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2 G_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-143-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-143">2 G_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and consequently a higher degradation of the tag bandwidth will be obtained. By introducing <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> into <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a> and expanding the susceptance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B = B_{\rm eq} +2 B_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-144-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-144">B = B_{\rm eq} +2 B_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (using <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\rm eq} = 1/(2\omega _{0}^{2} C_{c})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-145-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-145">L_{\rm eq} = 1/(2\omega _{0}^{2} C_{c})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the approximated bandwidth at a fixed value for the power reflection coefficient can be inferred, within the frequency range of validity of the proposed circuit approach.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Frequency Range of Validity of the Proposed Approach</h3><p>Let us now focus on the validity of the presented approach beyond the tag resonance frequency. As it has been pointed out, a T-match based tag designed following the steps indicated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3a" class="fulltext-link">Section III.A</a> will exhibit a frequency response centered at the desired frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Therefore, such a response will be similar to that of the proposed equivalent-circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>, using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> and designing the T-match network at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-147">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It follows that, in order to determine the frequency range of validity of the proposed approach, a comparison between these two frequency responses makes sense. Then, assuming that the tag antenna satisfies the required condition at the resonance frequency (see expression 16), an examination of condition <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> reveals that it will be satisfied within the whole UHF-RFID band provided <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert Z _{a}\vert \geq R_{a} (f_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">\vert Z _{a}\vert \geq R_{a} (f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It can be easily demonstrated that this condition holds true in the case of considering a canonic RLC series load as antenna impedance. Thus, in this particular case, condition <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> is accomplished in all frequencies and, consequently, the frequency limits around the tag resonance from which the proposed approach no longer predicts the frequency response of the designed tag are determined by <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a>. Therefore, in order to satisfy such condition within the entire UHF-RFID band, the frequency derivative of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\chi_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-149">\chi_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> must be small. Conversely, if the antenna impedance can be approximated by an RLC shunt load around the resonance frequency, both expressions <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> must be taken into account in order to obtain the frequency limits from which the proposed approach becomes invalid. This is exactly what happens by considering any general frequency dependent complex antenna impedance. Thus, in such cases, both the frequency derivatives of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\chi _{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-150">\chi _{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-151-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-151">R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should be small to enhance the frequency range of validity.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3d"><h3>D. Synthesis of a T-Match Based Tag Using a Resonant Antenna</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Model of an UHF-RFID T-match based tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
A simple method for the synthesis of T-match based tags using a resonant antenna is proposed in this section. In order to synthesize the T-match network, we start by considering a closed loop consisting of a narrow conductor strip (e.g., 0.2 mm width) connected to a differential port with impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-152-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-152">Z_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. This loop exhibits an inductive behavior at the UHF-RFID frequency band. To achieve the required dimensions for the loop inductance, a sweep of the length of the loop is carried out by means of electromagnetic simulations (by using the Agilent Momentum commercial software), until the resonance frequency appears at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0} - \Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-153-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-153">f_{0} - \Delta f</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Then, the inductance corresponding to one half of the loop must be divided into <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-154-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-154">L_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-155-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-155">L_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by connecting the antenna at the adequate position (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>). To this end, a sweep of the position of the antenna connection is carried out to achieve the calculated values for these inductances. The final position is obtained when the tag resonance reaches the desired frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-156-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-156">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Design of a Broadband UHF-RFID Tag Using the Proposed Method</h2></div><p>Let us now consider a typical integrated circuit for the RFID tag (the NXP UCODE G2XM chip). The impedance reported by the manufacturer of this integrated circuit is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm chip} = 16- j 148\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-157-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-157">Z_{\rm chip} = 16- j 148\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, at 915 MHz. As indicated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, the chip can be modeled by a parallel combination of a resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-158-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-158">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-159-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-159">C_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. These values were calculated from the input impedance of the chip transformed to its equivalent RC parallel circuit, giving <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{c} = 1385\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-160-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-160">R_{c} = 1385\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{c} = 1.16</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-161-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-161">C_{c} = 1.16</script></tex-math></inline-formula> pF. From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn16" href="#deqn16" class="fulltext-link">(16)</a> it follows that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">17\ \Omega \ll R_{a}(f_{0}) \leq 1385\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-162-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-162">17\ \Omega \ll R_{a}(f_{0}) \leq 1385\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Thus, the tag antenna has to be designed to exhibit an antenna resistance at the operating frequency according to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn16" href="#deqn16" class="fulltext-link">(16)</a>. As a proof of concept for the presented method, an antenna for tag implementation was designed on a commercial low loss microwave substrate, the Rogers RO3010 substrate with dielectric constant <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varepsilon_{r} = 10.2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-163-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-163">\varepsilon_{r} = 10.2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and thickness <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h = 0.254</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-164-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-164">h = 0.254</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm. As it was pointed out, the use of a resonant antenna becomes appropriate to ensure the validity of the presented approach around the operating frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-165-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-165">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The proposed antenna is a meandered coplanar strip, folded dipole working at the so called antenna mode <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_4">[25]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_4">[26]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_4">[27]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4">[28]</a>, which allows the antenna impedance (at least the imaginary part) to be approximated by the canonic RLC series load, around the antenna resonance frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-166-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-166">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The designed antenna exhibits a
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Input impedance of the designed tag antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Simulated power reflection coefficient of the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, by sweeping the antenna impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-167-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-167">Z_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 20 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-168-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-168">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to 1385 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-169-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-169">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
purely resistive impedance at the intermediate frequency, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} (f_{0}) = 220\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-170-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-170">R_{a} (f_{0}) = 220\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>). Then, in order to design the T-match network at the correct frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0} - \Delta f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-171-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-171">f_{0} - \Delta f</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the frequency shift was inferred by using expression <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqna4" href="#deqna4" class="fulltext-link">(A4)</a> and it was found to be 8 MHz. This result perfectly agrees with the shift obtained in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>, where a simulation (by means of the Agilent ADS circuit simulator) of the power reflection coefficient of the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>, using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> and designing the T-match network at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-172-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-172">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, with a sweep of the antenna impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{a} = R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-173-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-173">Z_{a} = R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 20 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-174-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-174">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to 1385 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-175-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-175">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is depicted. As expected in this analysis, perfect conjugate matching at the desired frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-176-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-176">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is achieved when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a} = R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-177-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-177">R_{a} = R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and, consequently, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{1} = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-178-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-178">L_{1} = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{2} = 1/(2\omega _{0}^{2} C_{c})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-179-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-179">L_{2} = 1/(2\omega _{0}^{2} C_{c})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This is because in this case, approximation <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> becomes an exact expression for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-180-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-180">L_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq} = 2 G_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-181-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-181">G_{\rm eq} = 2 G_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As it was previously predicted, a frequency shift of the tag resonance from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-182-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-182">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> toward higher frequencies and a reduction of the matching level at this frequency are observed as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-183-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-183">R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> decreases from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-184-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-184">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> that such frequency shift and matching level reduction at the resonance frequency become more significant as the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-185-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-185">R_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> moves away from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-186-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-186">R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Thus, the T-match network was designed at 890 MHz, which corresponds to 8 MHz below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-187-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-187">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12-13" href="#deqn12-13" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12-13" href="#deqn12-13" class="fulltext-link">(13)</a>, the elements of the T-match network where found to be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{1} = 8.3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-188-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-188">L_{1} = 8.3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> nH and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{2} = 5.5</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-189-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-189">L_{2} = 5.5</script></tex-math></inline-formula> nH. Then, the synthesis method explained in the previous section was applied. The layout of the designed tag is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10(a)</a>. The dimensions are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l =120</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-190-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-190">l =120</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w =30</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-191-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-191">w =30</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g =4.9</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-192-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-192">g =4.9</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">c =8.7</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-193-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-193">c =8.7</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{1} =12</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-194-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-194">d_{1} =12</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{2} =9</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-195-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-195">d_{2} =9</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{3} =9</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-196-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-196">d_{3} =9</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm. All the strips of the antenna have the same width (3 mm) and the width of the T-match network is 0.2 mm. The total length of the T-match closed loop was found to be 30 mm, and the tag antenna was connected to the loop at a distance of 10.2 mm from the chip.<p></p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>(a) Layout of the designed T-match based tag. (b) Electrical simulation of the return loss of the proposed equivalent-circuit (dash dot line) and electromagnetic simulation of the return loss of the designed tag (solid line).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The power reflection coefficient of the designed RFID tag is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10(b)</a>. It can be seen that conjugate matching is achieved at the intermediate frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-197-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-197">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the UHF-RFID frequency band. Very good agreement is observed between the power reflection coefficient obtained from the equivalent-circuit approach and the electromagnetic simulation within the entire UHF-RFID band except in the low frequency region. Although the tag antenna exhibits purely resistive impedance at the resonance frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-198-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-198">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the antenna resistance is not constant with frequency, as it is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. Hence, both conditions <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14-15" href="#deqn14-15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> must be examined to discuss the validity of the approach applied in this work within the UHF-RFID band, as it was mentioned in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3c" class="fulltext-link">Section III.C</a>. For the considered chip and antenna impedance, we obtain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert Z _{a}\vert \gg 61\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-199-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-199">\vert Z _{a}\vert \gg 61\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \chi _{a}\vert \leq 51\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-200-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-200">\vert \chi _{a}\vert \leq 51\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Thus, the condition for the antenna reactance is satisfied between 867 MHz and 930 MHz. However, although the condition for the absolute value of the antenna impedance is well satisfied at frequencies higher than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-201-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-201">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and in the vicinity, there is a frequency region within the low UHF-RFID band where such condition is less satisfied. Therefore, good agreement is expected between the power reflection coefficients of the equivalent-circuit approach and the electromagnetic response of the designed tag within the whole UHF-RFID band, except in the low frequency region.<p></p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>(a) Electric plane radiation pattern of the designed T-match based tag and (b) magnetic plane. The proposed tag has a radiation pattern similar to that of a conventional <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\lambda /2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-202-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-202">\lambda /2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dipole in the whole UHF-RFID band.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
As indicated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3b" class="fulltext-link">Section III.B</a>, by introducing <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> into <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a>, the approximated bandwidth at a fixed value for the power reflection coefficient can be predicted, within the frequency range of validity of the proposed circuit approach. Thus, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{-} 15</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-203-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-203">{-} 15</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dB bandwidth was found to be 35 MHz, which is similar to the obtained by means of the electromagnetic simulation of the designed tag (39 MHz). The simulated gain reaches the value of 1.8 dBi at the operating frequency and the radiation pattern is similar to that of a conventional <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\lambda /2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-204-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-204">\lambda /2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dipole in the whole UHF-RFID band, as it is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Fabrication and Measurement</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Theoretical Read Range</h3><p>To determine the performance of the tags, it is necessary to obtain the read range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_5a">[29]</a>, which can be calculated using the Friis free space formula as <disp-formula id="deqn18" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r = {\lambda\over 4\pi}\sqrt{{{\rm EIRP}\ G_{r} \tau\over P_{\rm chip}}} \eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-205-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-205">r = {\lambda\over 4\pi}\sqrt{{{\rm EIRP}\ G_{r} \tau\over P_{\rm chip}}} \eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">r = {\lambda\over 4\pi}\sqrt{{{\rm EIRP}\ G_{r} \tau\over P_{\rm chip}}} \eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</span></span></disp-formula>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677544/6655974/6655974-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>(a) Photograph of the fabricated RFID tag and (b) simulated and measured read range. The measured read ranges of the UPM Web tag (that uses the tag chip of our prototype), and the Alien ALN-9640 tag of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, are also shown for comparison purposes.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6655974/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\lambda</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-206-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-206">\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the wavelength and EIRP is the equivalent isotropically radiated power, determined by local country regulations (e.g., 3.3 W in Europe and 4 W in USA). <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-207-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-207">P_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the minimum threshold power necessary to activate the RFID chip, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-208-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-208">G_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of the receiving tag antenna, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-209-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-209">\tau</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the power transmission coefficient, which is related to the power reflection coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert s \vert^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-210-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-210">\vert s \vert^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau = (1- \vert s \vert^{2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-211-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-211">\tau = (1- \vert s \vert^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The tag gain and the power transmission coefficient are inferred from simulation, using as port impedance that of the chip. Despite the minimum power level necessary to activate the chip used in this work reported by the manufacturer is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip} = - 15</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-212-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-212">P_{\rm chip} = - 15</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dBm, a different threshold power was obtained in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_5a">[30]</a>. In such work it was found that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-213-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-213">P_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> exhibits a lower and frequency dependent value. Taken it into account and from electromagnetic and circuit co-simulation results, an evaluation of the theoretical read range was obtained and depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(b)</a>.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. Measured Read Range and Experimental Setup</h3><p>The RFID setup available in our laboratory has an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Agilent\ N5182A</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-214-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-214">Agilent\ N5182A</script></tex-math></inline-formula> vector signal generator, which creates RFID frames and plays the role of a reader with variable frequency and variable output power. Such generator is connected to a TEM cell by means of a circulator. The tag under test is located inside the TEM cell and it is excited by the frame created by the generator. Then the tag sends a backscatter signal to an Agilent N9020A signal analyzer through the circulator. At each frequency, the minimum power at the input of the TEM cell required to communicate with the tag is recorded. Finally, an electric probe is placed into the TEM cell to determine the root mean square of the incident electric field, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E_{\rm rms}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-215-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-215">E_{\rm rms}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, corresponding to the minimum power at each frequency. This electric field is related to the power delivered to the chip according to <disp-formula id="deqn19" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip} = SA_{\rm ef} \tau = {\vert {E_{\rm rms}} \vert^{2}\over \eta} {\lambda^{2}G_{r}\over 4\pi}\tau \eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-216-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-216">P_{\rm chip} = SA_{\rm ef} \tau = {\vert {E_{\rm rms}} \vert^{2}\over \eta} {\lambda^{2}G_{r}\over 4\pi}\tau \eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm chip} = SA_{\rm ef} \tau = {\vert {E_{\rm rms}} \vert^{2}\over \eta} {\lambda^{2}G_{r}\over 4\pi}\tau \eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-217-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-217">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the incident power density, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{\rm ef}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-218-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-218">A_{\rm ef}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the effective area of the tag antenna, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-219-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-219">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the wave impedance of free space. The measured read range can be inferred by introducing <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn19" href="#deqn19" class="fulltext-link">(19)</a> into <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn18" href="#deqn18" class="fulltext-link">(18)</a>, resulting the following expression <disp-formula id="deqn20" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r = {\sqrt {30\ {\rm EIRP}}\over E_{\rm rms}} \eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-220-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-220">r = {\sqrt {30\ {\rm EIRP}}\over E_{\rm rms}} \eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">r = {\sqrt {30\ {\rm EIRP}}\over E_{\rm rms}} \eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5c"><h3>C. Experimental Results</h3><p>The proposed RFID tag was fabricated and the read range was measured (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>) through the procedure explained above. Very good agreement between the theoretical and measured read ranges can be observed. The fabricated tag exhibits a significant read range within the whole UHF-RFID band (840–960 MHz), with a peak value of 11 m at 898 MHz. The read range of a commercially available tag (UPM Web) that uses the NXP UCODE G2XM chip and the T-match network is also shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(b)</a> for comparison purposes. It can be seen that our fabricated tag exhibits a substantially superior read range in the whole UHF-RFID band. Despite the fact that comparing RFID tags only makes sense if they use the same chip (the chip impedance and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-221-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-221">P_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are key parameters in determining the read range), we have also included in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(b)</a> the read range of the commercial tag Alien ALN-9640 (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>). Such tag uses a chip (the Alien Higgs 3) with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip} = - 18</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-222-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-222">P_{\rm chip} = - 18</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dBm, whereas <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm chip} = - 15</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-223-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-223">P_{\rm chip} = - 15</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dBm for the NXP UCODE G2XM chip (according to the manufacturer specifications). In spite of this significant difference in the threshold power, the read range at 898 MHz is comparable in both the ALN-9640 tag and our proposed tag. Therefore, the proposed approach for the design of global band UHF-RFID tags is simple and competitive in terms of the main figure of merit: the read range.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this paper, a systematic and simple method for the design of UHF-RFID tags, based on the T-match network, has been introduced. This method is based on a new equivalent- circuit model for the RFID tag that includes the tag antenna, the chip and the matching network. The main advantage of this method, in comparison with the methods reported in the literature, is the simplicity in synthesizing the T-match network required to achieve a broad band frequency response with conjugate matching between the chip and the antenna. Nevertheless, such antenna must be previously designed to exhibit a self-resonance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-224-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-224">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. As a proof of concept, a global band tag has been designed using this method, and the read range of the fabricated prototype has been measured and compared to those of commercially available tags. The results reveal that the designed tag is very competitive, and point out that the proposed circuit-based approach is very useful for the synthesis of T-match based tags.</p></div>

<div class="section" id="app1"><h2></h2><h1> Appendix</h1><div class="section_2" id="app1a"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION A.</div><h2>Calculation of the Frequency shift of the Tag Resonance</h2></div><p>Let us consider the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, where the tag antenna has a purely resistive impedance such that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{a} = R_{a} \leq R_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-225-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-225">Z_{a} = R_{a} \leq R_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The power reflection coefficient, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert s \vert^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-248-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-248">\vert s \vert^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, from the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> is given by expression <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a>. By forcing the frequency derivative of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a> to be zero, it is found that <disp-formula id="deqnB1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2B{B}'G_{\rm eq} = {G}'_{\rm eq} \left({B^{2} + 4G_{\rm chip}^{2} - G_{\rm eq}^{2}}\right) \eqno{\hbox{(B1)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-249-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-249">2B{B}'G_{\rm eq} = {G}'_{\rm eq} \left({B^{2} + 4G_{\rm chip}^{2} - G_{\rm eq}^{2}}\right) \eqno{\hbox{(B1)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">2B{B}'G_{\rm eq} = {G}'_{\rm eq} \left({B^{2} + 4G_{\rm chip}^{2} - G_{\rm eq}^{2}}\right) \eqno{\hbox{(B1)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B'</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-250-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-250">B'</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G'_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-251-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-251">G'_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are the frequency derivatives of the susceptance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-252-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-252">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the conductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-253-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-253">G_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. Notice that all the parameters in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnB1" href="#deqnB1" class="fulltext-link">(B1)</a> are frequency dependent functions, except <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-254-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-254">G_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It can be deduced that <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqnB1" href="#deqnB1" class="fulltext-link">(B1)</a> is satisfied at that frequency when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-255-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-255">B = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, provided that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{\rm eq} = 2 G_{\rm chip}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-256-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-256">G_{\rm eq} = 2 G_{\rm chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div></div>
</div></div>

He is now very active in the field of metamaterials and their application to the miniaturization and optimization of microwave circuits and antennas.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">Dr. Martı´n is the head of the Microwave and Millimeter Wave Engineering Group (GEMMA Group) at UAB, and director of CIMITEC, a research Center on Metamaterials supported by TECNIO (Generalitat de Catalunya). He has organized several international events related to metamaterials, including Workshops at the IEEE International Microwave Symposium (2005 and 2007) and European Microwave Conference (2009). He has acted as Guest Editor for three Special Issues on Metamaterials in three International Journals. He has authored and co-authored over 350 technical conference, letter and journal papers and he is co-author of the monograph on Metamaterials entitled Metamaterials with Negative Parameters: Theory, Design and Microwave Applications (Wiley, 2013). He has filed several patents on metamaterials and has headed several Development Contracts. Among his distinctions, he has received the 2006 Duran Farell Prize for Technological Research, he holds the Parc de Recerca UAB—Santander Technology Transfer Chair, and he has been the recipient of an ICREA ACADEMIA Award.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p -->

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

The great majority of commercial UHF-RFID tags are based on dipole antennas using a modification of a T-match network. The literature contains examples of models that describe the T-match, but they are not sufficiently accurate to synthesize the tag geometry. Using the proposed methodology, a global band UHF-RFID tag based on a folded dipole antenna and matched to the RFID integrated circuit by means of a T-match network is designed and fabricated. Very good agreement between the measured and simulated read range is achieved within the entire UHF-RFID band, which reveals that the proposed method is amenable for accurate analysis and synthesis of
